```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- tabako: tobacco, cigarette
- aienka: heavy smoker, habitual smoker
- shigaretto: cigarette
- tabakokeesu: tobacco case
- shigarettopeepaa: cigarette paper

TONE HINT:
- shigarettokeesu: cigarette case
```

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.
```

### 6. `case-06-concentration` — Mental health/Neurological (concentration)

**Input:** `JAP: shuinbun wo yondari miru koto shuuchu dekimasen ka`

```
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

Output: I have chest pain.

Output: I have no allergies.
```

### 13. `case-13-early-satiety` — Post-prandial fullness / Weight issues

```
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.
```

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



TONE HINT:
- iwakan: uncomfortable feeling

Input: nennen hakike hidoi no to chokkan dake desu ato yoko ni natte okiagaru toki ya tatte suwatte tachi agaru toki ni chotto memai yousuruni desu yonaka mo katai kanji shite shitsumon i ga itai desu senjutsu kuroi ben deta desu ga nani ka warui koto da to omoimasu ka
Output: /no_think
```

#### Tone / Pragmatic Context Hint

| 0.659 | `yoreba` | — | according to |

<details>
<summary>Full prompt sent to Ollama (click to expand)</summary>

```
TASK:
Translate the following Japanese (romaji) dialogue into natural English.

You are an interpreter. The speaker may be a Japanese patient describing symptoms or a doctor asking screening questions.

RULES:
- Use FIRST PERSON ("I", "my", "I feel") when the speaker is a patient. 
- Use natural medical questioning ("Have you...", "Do you fee...") when the speaker is a doctor.
- Translate faithfully. Do NOT add information that is not present.
- If input is unnatural or fragmented, reconstruct into natural English meaning using standard Japanese grammar.
- CLINICAL PRIORITY: If a term is ambiguous, prioritize the most clinical or medical interpretation (e.g., "gein" as "cause", not "performance").
- Output ONLY the English sentence — no labels, no explanation, no Japanese.

EXAMPLES:
Input: mune itai
Output: I have chest pain.

Input: arerugi nai
Output: I have no allergies.

Input: zutsu hidoisugite ugokenai
Output: My headache is so bad I can't move.



MEDICAL GLOSSARY HINTS:
- uranai: fortune-telling, divination
- korera: cholera
- imyou: another name, nickname
- warui: bad, poor

TONE HINT:
- yoreba: according to

Input: wakatta sensei korera ijyou warukunai uranai to iinokosu desu ga sugi no youyaku itsu desuka saisho chichi no hi de happyoukai aru no de
Output: /no_think
```

</details>

#### LLM Output

> I understand, Doctor. I don't think I have cholera, but I'm worried because there's a funeral for my father on the first day of the new year.
